17NR2F1 stratifies dormant disseminated tumor cells in breast cancer patients | Breast Cancer Research | Full Text</title>

22 <meta name="citation_abstract" content="The presence of disseminated tumor cells (DTCs) in bone marrow (BM) is an independent prognostic factor in early breast cancer but does not uniformly predict outcome. Tumor cells can persist in a quiescent state over time, but clinical studies of markers predicting the awakening potential of DTCs are lacking. Recently, experiments have shown that NR2F1 (COUP-TF1) plays a key role in dormancy signaling. We analyzed the NR2F1 expression in DTCs by double immunofluorescence (DIF) staining of extra cytospins prepared from 114 BM samples from 86 selected DTC-positive breast cancer patients. Samples collected at two or more time points were available for 24 patients. Fifteen samples were also analyzed for the proliferation marker Ki67. Of the patients with detectable DTCs by DIF, 27% had &#8805;&#8201;50% NR2F1high DTCs, chosen a priori as the cut-off for &#8220;dormant profile&#8221; classification. All patients with systemic relapse within 12&#160;months after BM aspiration carried &#8804;&#8201;1% NR2F1high DTCs, including patients who transitioned from having NR2F1high-expressing DTCs in previous BM samples. Of the patients with serial samples, half of those with no relapse at follow-up had &#8805;&#8201;50% NR2F1high DTCs in the last BM aspiration analyzed. Among the 18 relapse-free patients at the time of the last DTC-positive BM aspiration with no subsequent BM analysis performed, distant disease-free intervals were favorable for patients carrying &#8805;&#8201;50% NR2F1high DTCs compared with those with predominantly NR2F1low DTCs (p&#8201;=&#8201;0.007, log-rank). No survival difference was observed by classification according to Ki67-expressing DTCs (p&#8201;=&#8201;0.520). Our study translates findings from basic biological analysis of DTC dormancy to the clinical situation and supports further clinical studies of NR2F1 as a marker of dormancy."/>

599 <meta property="og:url" content="https://breast-cancer-research.biomedcentral.com/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0"/>

600

601 <meta property="og:type" content="article"/>

602

603 <meta property="og:site_name" content="BioMed Central"/>

604

605 <meta property="og:title" content="NR2F1 stratifies dormant disseminated tumor cells in breast cancer patients - Breast Cancer Research"/>

606

607 <meta property="og:description" content="Background The presence of disseminated tumor cells (DTCs) in bone marrow (BM) is an independent prognostic factor in early breast cancer but does not uniformly predict outcome. Tumor cells can persist in a quiescent state over time, but clinical studies of markers predicting the awakening potential of DTCs are lacking. Recently, experiments have shown that NR2F1 (COUP-TF1) plays a key role in dormancy signaling. Methods We analyzed the NR2F1 expression in DTCs by double immunofluorescence (DIF) staining of extra cytospins prepared from 114 BM samples from 86 selected DTC-positive breast cancer patients. Samples collected at two or more time points were available for 24 patients. Fifteen samples were also analyzed for the proliferation marker Ki67. Results Of the patients with detectable DTCs by DIF, 27% had &#8805;&#8201;50% NR2F1high DTCs, chosen a priori as the cut-off for &#8220;dormant profile&#8221; classification. All patients with systemic relapse within 12 months after BM aspiration carried &#8804;&#8201;1% NR2F1high DTCs, including patients who transitioned from having NR2F1high-expressing DTCs in previous BM samples. Of the patients with serial samples, half of those with no relapse at follow-up had &#8805;&#8201;50% NR2F1high DTCs in the last BM aspiration analyzed. Among the 18 relapse-free patients at the time of the last DTC-positive BM aspiration with no subsequent BM analysis performed, distant disease-free intervals were favorable for patients carrying &#8805;&#8201;50% NR2F1high DTCs compared with those with predominantly NR2F1low DTCs (p&#8201;=&#8201;0.007, log-rank). No survival difference was observed by classification according to Ki67-expressing DTCs (p&#8201;=&#8201;0.520). Conclusions Our study translates findings from basic biological analysis of DTC dormancy to the clinical situation and supports further clinical studies of NR2F1 as a marker of dormancy."/>

608

1631 <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en">

1632<div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section">

1633<h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">

1634Abstract</h2>

1635<div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content">

1636<h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" data-test="abstract-sub-heading">

1637Background</h3>

1638<p>

1639The presence of disseminated tumor cells (DTCs) in bone marrow (BM) is an independent prognostic factor in early breast cancer but does not uniformly predict outcome. Tumor cells can persist in a quiescent state over time, but clinical studies of markers predicting the awakening potential of DTCs are lacking. Recently, experiments have shown that NR2F1 (COUP-TF1) plays a key role in dormancy signaling.</p>

1640<h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" data-test="abstract-sub-heading">

1641Methods</h3>

1642<p>

1643We analyzed the NR2F1 expression in DTCs by double immunofluorescence (DIF) staining of extra cytospins prepared from 114 BM samples from 86 selected DTC-positive breast cancer patients. Samples collected at two or more time points were available for 24 patients. Fifteen samples were also analyzed for the proliferation marker Ki67.</p>

1644<h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" data-test="abstract-sub-heading">

1645Results</h3>

1646<p>

1647Of the patients with detectable DTCs by DIF, 27% had 50% NR2F1<sup>

1648high</sup>

1649 DTCs, chosen a priori as the cut-off for dormant profile classification. All patients with systemic relapse within 12months after BM aspiration carried 1% NR2F1<sup>

1650high</sup>

1651 DTCs, including patients who transitioned from having NR2F1<sup>

1652high</sup>

1653-expressing DTCs in previous BM samples. Of the patients with serial samples, half of those with no relapse at follow-up had 50% NR2F1<sup>

1654high</sup>

1655 DTCs in the last BM aspiration analyzed. Among the 18 relapse-free patients at the time of the last DTC-positive BM aspiration with no subsequent BM analysis performed, distant disease-free intervals were favorable for patients carrying 50% NR2F1<sup>

1656high</sup>

1657 DTCs compared with those with predominantly NR2F1<sup>

1658low</sup>

1659 DTCs (<i>

1660p</i>

1661=0.007, log-rank). No survival difference was observed by classification according to Ki67-expressing DTCs (<i>

1662p</i>

1663=0.520).</p>

1664<h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" data-test="abstract-sub-heading">

1665Conclusions</h3>

1666<p>

1667Our study translates findings from basic biological analysis of DTC dormancy to the clinical situation and supports further clinical studies of NR2F1 as a marker of dormancy.</p>

1668</div>

1669</div>

1670</section>

1671

1672

1673

1674

1675

1676 <section data-title="Background">

1677<div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section">

1678<h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">

1679Background</h2>

1680<div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content">

1681<p>

1682Breast cancer patients may experience relapse and subsequent death from the disease many years after primary treatment. This indicates an ability of occult cancer cells to survive in a non- or slow-proliferating state, retaining a potential for progression and proliferation at a later time point [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Linde N, Fluegen G, Aguirre-Ghiso JA. The relationship between dormant cancer cells and their microenvironment. Adv Cancer Res. 2016;132:4571." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e961">

16831</a>

1684, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Aguirre-Ghiso JA, Bragado P, Sosa MS. Metastasis awakening: targeting dormant cancer. Nat Med. 2013;19(3):2767." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e964">

16852</a>

1686]. The window of time represented by such minimal residual disease (MRD) represents a possibility for therapeutic intervention to prevent development of future metastasis rather than treat overt metastasis. However, the biology of the population of residual disseminated tumor cells (DTCs) is poorly understood. Large studies have shown the presence of DTCs in bone marrow (BM) to be a strong predictor of recurrence over the next 5years [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Braun S, Vogl FD, Naume B, Janni W, Osborne MP, Coombes RC, Schlimok G, Diel IJ, Gerber B, Gebauer G, et al. A pooled analysis of bone marrow micrometastasis in breast cancer. N Engl J Med. 2005;353(8):793802." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e967">

16873</a>

1688, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Janni W, Vogl FD, Wiedswang G, Synnestvedt M, Fehm T, Juckstock J, Borgen E, Rack B, Braun S, Sommer H, et al. Persistence of disseminated tumor cells in the bone marrow of breast cancer patients predicts increased risk for relapsea European pooled analysis. Clin Cancer Res. 2011;17(9):296776." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e970">

16894</a>

1690]. However, about 60% of the DTC-positive patients remained relapse-free until the end of the follow-up period. Consequently, there is an urgent need for markers to disclose the functional state of DTCs and evaluate their progression potential. Such markers may help us to understand the biology of dormant DTCs in patients and as decision-making tools for current and new therapies.</p>

1691<p>

1692Our experimental model studies of DTC dormancy revealed that NR2F1, an orphan nuclear receptor of the retinoic acid receptor family, is commonly downregulated in human cancer and metastatic tissues [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Adam AP, George A, Schewe D, Bragado P, Iglesias BV, Ranganathan AC, Kourtidis A, Conklin DS, Aguirre-Ghiso JA. Computational identification of a p38SAPK-regulated transcription factor network required for tumor cell quiescence. Cancer Res. 2009;69(14):566472." href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e976">

16935</a>

1694,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Sosa MS, Parikh F, Maia AG, Estrada Y, Bosch A, Bragado P, Ekpin E, George A, Zheng Y, Lam HM, et al. NR2F1 controls tumour cell dormancy via SOX9- and RARbeta-driven quiescence programmes. Nat Commun. 2015;6:6170." href="#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e976_1">

16956</a>

1696,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Sosa MS. Dormancy programs as emerging antimetastasis therapeutic alternatives. Mol Cell Oncol. 2016;3(1):e1029062." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e979">

16977</a>

1698]. In contrast, in a PDX model of squamous carcinoma, NR2F1 was upregulated in the DTCs that entered spontaneous dormancy [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Sosa MS, Parikh F, Maia AG, Estrada Y, Bosch A, Bragado P, Ekpin E, George A, Zheng Y, Lam HM, et al. NR2F1 controls tumour cell dormancy via SOX9- and RARbeta-driven quiescence programmes. Nat Commun. 2015;6:6170." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e982">

16996</a>

1700], and additional results suggested that NR2F1 may pinpoint dormant DTCs in different cancer types [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Sosa MS, Parikh F, Maia AG, Estrada Y, Bosch A, Bragado P, Ekpin E, George A, Zheng Y, Lam HM, et al. NR2F1 controls tumour cell dormancy via SOX9- and RARbeta-driven quiescence programmes. Nat Commun. 2015;6:6170." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e985">

17016</a>

1702]. DTC analysis in the experimental models indicated that when 4050% of DTCs displayed nuclear NR2F1, this correlated with quiescence markers, other dormancy markers such as DEC2 and SOX9, and lack of proliferation [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Sosa MS, Parikh F, Maia AG, Estrada Y, Bosch A, Bragado P, Ekpin E, George A, Zheng Y, Lam HM, et al. NR2F1 controls tumour cell dormancy via SOX9- and RARbeta-driven quiescence programmes. Nat Commun. 2015;6:6170." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e988">

17036</a>

1704, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Fluegen G, Avivar-Valderas A, Wang Y, Padgen MR, Williams JK, Nobre AR, Calvo V, Cheung JF, Bravo-Cordero JJ, Entenberg D, et al. Phenotypic heterogeneity of disseminated tumour cells is preset by primary tumour hypoxic microenvironments. Nat Cell Biol. 2017;19(2):12032." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e992">

17058</a>

1706]. In addition, a frequency of less than 20% of DTCs positive for NR2F1 correlated with a lack of expression of the above markers of dormancy, quiescence, and proliferation. Metastatic and local recurrence samples in head and neck squamous cell carcinoma that clearly escaped dormancy showed less than 5% of tumor cells positive for NR2F1 (supplementing data in [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Sosa MS, Parikh F, Maia AG, Estrada Y, Bosch A, Bragado P, Ekpin E, George A, Zheng Y, Lam HM, et al. NR2F1 controls tumour cell dormancy via SOX9- and RARbeta-driven quiescence programmes. Nat Commun. 2015;6:6170." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e995">

17076</a>

1708]). Furthermore, dormant DTCs upregulated genes linked to NR2F1 signaling, including several retinoic acid-regulated genes [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Sosa MS, Parikh F, Maia AG, Estrada Y, Bosch A, Bragado P, Ekpin E, George A, Zheng Y, Lam HM, et al. NR2F1 controls tumour cell dormancy via SOX9- and RARbeta-driven quiescence programmes. Nat Commun. 2015;6:6170." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e998">

17096</a>

1710]. In prostate cancer samples, we found that 4347% of DTCs from patients with no evidence of disease after many years of relapse-free follow-up showed NR2F1 mRNA upregulation, compared with 10% of the DTCs in advanced prostate cancer [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Sosa MS, Parikh F, Maia AG, Estrada Y, Bosch A, Bragado P, Ekpin E, George A, Zheng Y, Lam HM, et al. NR2F1 controls tumour cell dormancy via SOX9- and RARbeta-driven quiescence programmes. Nat Commun. 2015;6:6170." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1001">

17116</a>

1712]. Altogether, these results support further testing of NR2F1 as a dormancy marker in solitary DTCs from clinical samples, including assessment of cut-off values to classify patients according to NR2F1 expression.</p>

1713<p>

1714Three Norwegian early breast cancer cohorts were previously analyzed for DTCs in the BM [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Mathiesen RR, Borgen E, Renolen A, Lokkevik E, Nesland JM, Anker G, Ostenstad B, Lundgren S, Risberg T, Mjaaland I, et al. 17159</a>

1716,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wiedswang G, Borgen E, Karesen R, Kvalheim G, Nesland JM, Qvist H, Schlichting E, Sauer T, Janbu J, Harbitz T, et al. Detection of isolated tumor cells in bone marrow is an independent prognostic factor in breast cancer. J Clin Oncol. 2003;21(18):346978." href="#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1007_1">

171710</a>

1718,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wiedswang G, Borgen E, Karesen R, Qvist H, Janbu J, Kvalheim G, Nesland JM, Naume B. 172112</a>

172514</a>

1726] using the standard immunocytochemical method(standard ICC) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Borgen E, Naume B, Nesland JM, Kvalheim G, Beiske K, Fodstad O, Diel I, Solomayer EF, Theocharous P, Coombes RC, et al. 172715</a>

1728, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Fehm T, Braun S, Muller V, Janni W, Gebauer G, Marth C, Schindlbeck C, Wallwiener D, Borgen E, Naume B, et al. 172916</a>

1730]. Clinical follow-up identified the presence of DTCs to be a significant, independent predictor of unfavorable outcome [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Mathiesen RR, Borgen E, Renolen A, Lokkevik E, Nesland JM, Anker G, Ostenstad B, Lundgren S, Risberg T, Mjaaland I, et al. Breast Cancer Res. 2012;14(4):R117." href="#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1019">

17319</a>

1732,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wiedswang G, Borgen E, Karesen R, Kvalheim G, Nesland JM, Qvist H, Schlichting E, Sauer T, Janbu J, Harbitz T, et al. Detection of isolated tumor cells in bone marrow is an independent prognostic factor in breast cancer. J Clin Oncol. 2003;21(18):346978." href="#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1019_1">

173310</a>

1734,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Wiedswang G, Borgen E, Karesen R, Qvist H, Janbu J, Kvalheim G, Nesland JM, Naume B. Isolated tumor cells in bone marrow three years after diagnosis in disease-free breast cancer patients predict unfavorable clinical outcome. Clin Cancer Res. 2004;10(16):53428." href="#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1019_2">

173511</a>

1736,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Naume B, Synnestvedt M, Falk RS, Wiedswang G, Weyde K, Risberg T, Kersten C, Mjaaland I, Vindi L, Sommer HH, et al. Clinical outcome with correlation to disseminated tumor cell (DTC) status after DTC-guided secondary adjuvant treatment with docetaxel in early breast cancer. J Clin Oncol. 2014;32(34):384857." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1023">

173712</a>

1738]. To explore the functional state of the DTCs, we optimized double immunofluorescence (DIF) protocols for detection of NR2F1 and Ki67 on DTCs and analyzed selected BM samples from these three breast cancer cohortswith comparison to clinical parameters. Our study is the first to translate findings from basic biological mechanism analysis of DTC dormancy to the clinical situation.</p>

1747<h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec3">

1748Breast cancer patient cohorts</h3>

1749<p>

1750The patient material includes cytospins with BM mononuclear cells (MNCs) from breast cancer patients included in one of three different Norwegian studies in the period from 1995 to 2008. An overview of the studies and included patients is presented in Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Fig1">

17511</a>

1752, and below.</p>

1785<p>

1786The NeoTax study enrolled 260 patients with stage III/IV breast cancer between 1997 and 2003 and randomly allocated them to treatment with paclitaxel or epirubicin, with a crossover between treatment arms if there was no response [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Mathiesen RR, Borgen E, Renolen A, Lokkevik E, Nesland JM, Anker G, Ostenstad B, Lundgren S, Risberg T, Mjaaland I, et al. Persistence of disseminated tumor cells after neoadjuvant treatment for locally advanced breast cancer predicts poor survival. Breast Cancer Res. 2012;14(4):R117." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1061">

17879</a>

1788, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Chrisanthar R, Knappskog S, Lokkevik E, Anker G, Ostenstad B, Lundgren S, Berge EO, Risberg T, Mjaaland I, Maehle L, et al. CHEK2 mutations affecting kinase activity together with mutations in TP53 indicate a functional pathway associated with resistance to epirubicin in primary breast cancer. PLoS One. 2008;3(8):e3062." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1064">

178913</a>

1790, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Chrisanthar R, Knappskog S, Lokkevik E, Anker G, Ostenstad B, Lundgren S, Risberg T, Mjaaland I, Skjonsberg G, Aas T, et al. Predictive and prognostic impact of TP53 mutations and MDM2 promoter genotype in primary breast cancer patients treated with epirubicin or paclitaxel. PLoS One. 2011;6(4):e19249." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1067">

179114</a>

1792]. Stage IV patients were included only ifthey harbored a locally advanced disease (T3/T4 and/or N2/N3) with limited distant metastases. After chemotherapy, mastectomy with axillary clearance was performed, followed by radiotherapy and antihormonal therapy when estrogen receptor (ER)-positive. BM aspirations for DTC analysis were performed prior to the start of chemotherapy (BM1), at surgery (BM2), and 12months after randomization (BM3).</p>

1793<p>

1794The Oslo1 observational study enrolled 920 patients with stage I/II breast cancer between 1995 and 1998, and submitted them to standard adjuvant therapy, antihormonal therapy, and radiotherapy according to Norwegian guidelines at the time of the study. BM aspirations for DTC analysis were performed at surgery (BM1), and after 3years of follow-up (for about one-third of the patients; BM2) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Wiedswang G, Borgen E, Karesen R, Kvalheim G, Nesland JM, Qvist H, Schlichting E, Sauer T, Janbu J, Harbitz T, et al. Detection of isolated tumor cells in bone marrow is an independent prognostic factor in breast cancer. J Clin Oncol. 2003;21(18):346978." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1073">

179510</a>

1796, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Wiedswang G, Borgen E, Karesen R, Qvist H, Janbu J, Kvalheim G, Nesland JM, Naume B. Isolated tumor cells in bone marrow three years after diagnosis in disease-free breast cancer patients predict unfavorable clinical outcome. Clin Cancer Res. 2004;10(16):53428." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1076">

179711</a>

1798].</p>

1799<p>

1800The SATT study [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Naume B, Synnestvedt M, Falk RS, Wiedswang G, Weyde K, Risberg T, Kersten C, Mjaaland I, Vindi L, Sommer HH, et al. Clinical outcome with correlation to disseminated tumor cell (DTC) status after DTC-guided secondary adjuvant treatment with docetaxel in early breast cancer. J Clin Oncol. 2014;32(34):384857." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1082">

180112</a>

1802, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Synnestvedt M, Borgen E, Wist E, Wiedswang G, Weyde K, Risberg T, Kersten C, Mjaaland I, Vindi L, Schirmer C, et al. Disseminated tumor cells as selection marker and monitoring tool for secondary adjuvant treatment in early breast cancer. Descriptive results from an intervention study. BMC Cancer. 2012;12:616." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1085">

180317</a>

1804] enrolled 1121 patients with operable breast cancer between 2003 and 2008. In addition to chemotherapy, patients received antihormonal therapy, radiotherapy, and from 2005 also herceptin if HER2-positive, according to Norwegian guidelines at the time of the study. Patients who had completed six cycles of standard adjuvant fluorouracil, epirubicin, and cyclophosphamide (FEC) chemotherapy underwent BM aspiration 2 to 3months (BM1) and 8 to 9months (BM2) after FEC. The presence of DTCs in BM was determined by immunocytochemistry. If one or more DTCs were present at BM2, six cycles of docetaxel (100mg/m<sup>

18052</sup>

1806, once every 3weeks) were administered, followed by DTC analysis 1 and 13months after the last docetaxel infusion (BM3 and BM4).</p>

1807<h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4">

1808Preparation of bone marrow mononuclear cell samples and cytospins</h3>

1809<p>

1810Bone marrow was aspirated in heparin (1000IE/ml; 0.5ml per 10ml BM) from iliac crests bilaterally under local anesthesia (510ml per site) and pooled into one tube. The samples were stored at room temperature until processing within 24h. The aspirates were diluted 1:1 in phosphate-buffered saline (PBS; Gibco, Life Technologies) and separated by density centrifugation using Lymphoprep (Axis-Shield, Oslo, Norway). Mononuclear cells were collected from the interphase layer, washed in 1% fetal calf serum in PBS (Gibco), and resuspended to 110<sup>

18116</sup>

1812 cells/mL. Cytospins were prepared by centrifugation of the BM MNCs down to poly-<span class="u-small-caps">

1813l</span>

1814-lysine-coated glass slides (510<sup>

18155</sup>

1816 MNCs/slide) in a Hettich cytocentrifuge (Tutlingen, Germany), air-dried at room temperature overnight, and stored at 80C until immunostaining.</p>

1817<h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5">

1818Patient material</h3>

1819<p>

1820For all the studies, the large majority of DTC-positive samples had only one detectable DTC in the original standard ICC analysis. A minority of the original samples contained 25 up to several thousand DTCs. For the present study, stored frozen cytospins prepared in parallel to the cytospins used for the initial (original) analysis were used when available. For some samples, viable BM MNCs stored in liquid nitrogen were thawed and new cytospins were prepared. To increase the chance of detecting DTCs in the study samples, we primarily selected patients having 3 DTCs per 210<sup>

18216</sup>

1822 BM MNCs by the original DTC analysis. However, patients with 02 DTCs were also included. When available, we prioritized BM from patients where successive samples over time were available. For some patients, no more spare BM was available for the present analysis. Normally, two cytospins containing in total 110<sup>

18236</sup>

1824 BM MNCs with adequate staining quality were analyzed for NR2F1 and for Ki67. The staining of samples and scoring of Ki67 and NR2F1 were performed by EB and MCR without access to the clinical database for the trials or information about time to relapse.</p>

1825<p>

1826Based on this, the present study included cytospins of BM MNCs from a total of 86 patients categorized as DTC-positive by the original gold standard DTC analysis performed prospectively within the original studies (DTC-positivity in at least one original sample if more than one BM aspiration was performed; ICC APAAP technique, four cytospins, 210<sup>

18276</sup>

1828 BM MNCs analyzed) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Borgen E, Naume B, Nesland JM, Kvalheim G, Beiske K, Fodstad O, Diel I, Solomayer EF, Theocharous P, Coombes RC, et al. Standardization of the immunocytochemical detection of cancer cells in BM and blood: I. Establishment of objective criteria for the evaluation of immunostained cells. Cytotherapy. 1999;1(5):37788." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1122">

182915</a>

1830, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Fehm T, Braun S, Muller V, Janni W, Gebauer G, Marth C, Schindlbeck C, Wallwiener D, Borgen E, Naume B, et al. A concept for the standardized detection of disseminated tumor cells in bone marrow from patients with primary breast cancer and its clinical implementation. Cancer. 2006;107(5):88592." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1125">

183116</a>

1832], of which 13 were included in Oslo1, 38 in the NeoTax study, and 35 in the SATT study (Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Fig1">

18331</a>

1834). For 24 of these patients, successive analyses from two or three time points were analyzed (20 at two time points and 4 at three time points). Samples from 11 patients with no detectable DTCs by the original DTC analysis were also included. In total, 127 samples were analyzed (all presented in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM1">

18351</a>

1836: Table S1).</p>

1837<h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6">

1838NR2F1/Ki67 and AE1AE3 double immunofluorescence staining protocol</h3>

1839<p>

1840Double immunofluorescence was performed using the broad-specter anticytokeratin (anti-CK) monoclonal antibodies (mAbs) AE1/AE3 combined with anti-COUP TF1/NR2F1 for expression of dormancy. From a selection of the samples, parallel (additional) cytospins were available and DIF was performed using anti-CK mAbs AE1/AE3 combined with the marker Ki67 for proliferation expression. Cytospins (0.510<sup>

18416</sup>

1842 MNCs/slide) were fixed for 12min in methanol/acetone (1:1) at room temperature and briefly air-dried, permeabilized in Triton X-100 (0.1% in PBS (DPBS Gibco-CaCl<sub>

18432</sub>

1844/MgCl<sub>

18452</sub>

1846)) for 7min, followed by a wash in PBS. The slides were then incubated for 45min with one of the following mAbs: NR2F1 Anti-COUP TF1 (Abcam Ab 41,858; 10g/mL) or anti-Ki67 clone MIB-1 (DAKO M7240; 1.15g/mL). They were subsequently labelled with Alexa Fluor 488 goat anti-mouse IgG (H+L) (Molecular Probes 11029; 4g/mL) and incubated for 45min. To block for cross-reactions (Ki67) the slides were then incubated with a mouse mAb MOPC21 (Sigma-Aldrich M9269; 20g/mL) for 20min. Finally, a combination of the two anti-CK mAbs AE1 and AE3 (Chemicon Millipore mAbs 1611/1612) were added, fluorescently labelled by Zenon 555 (2g of the AE1/AE3 combination per slide was labeled by the Zenon 555 mouse IgG labeling kit (Life technologies Molecular Probes, Z25005) diluted to 20g/mL), and the slides were incubated for 45min. Slides were washed 25 min in PBS, then sealed with ProLong Gold antifade reagent with DAPI (Life technologies P36931) and cover-slipped. Throughout the protocol, the slides were washed 25 min in PBS after each antibody incubation step. All antibodies were diluted in PBS/0.5% Tween20/5% normal goat serum. Cytospins (0.510<sup>

18476</sup>

1848 MNCs/slide) spiked with 1% MCF7 or SKBR3 breast cancer cell line cells were used as positive controls for the anti-CK staining and for optimization of the DIF protocols. Among the normal BM cells in the patient cytospins there were both Ki67-positive cells and cells with 05 small NR2F1 signals (see a more detailed description below), serving as internal positive controls for the NR2F1 staining.</p>

1849<h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7">

1850Scoring of individual DTCs and NR2F1/Ki67 expression</h3>

1851<p>

1852Stained cells were identified by manual screening in a Leica Microsystems DMI6000B fluorescence microscope, using 20, 40, and 63 objectives. Only AE1/AE3-positive cells with a morphology compatible with tumor cells were scored as DTCs [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Borgen E, Naume B, Nesland JM, Kvalheim G, Beiske K, Fodstad O, Diel I, Solomayer EF, Theocharous P, Coombes RC, et al. Standardization of the immunocytochemical detection of cancer cells in BM and blood: I. Establishment of objective criteria for the evaluation of immunostained cells. Cytotherapy. 1999;1(5):37788." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1159">

185315</a>

1854, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Fehm T, Braun S, Muller V, Janni W, Gebauer G, Marth C, Schindlbeck C, Wallwiener D, Borgen E, Naume B, et al. A concept for the standardized detection of disseminated tumor cells in bone marrow from patients with primary breast cancer and its clinical implementation. Cancer. 2006;107(5):88592." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1162">

185516</a>

1856].</p>

1857<p>

1858The definitions of DTC as either NR2F1<sup>

1859low</sup>

1860 or NR2F1<sup>

1861high</sup>

1862 used in this study were determined prior to starting the screening of the patient samples. When optimizing the AE1AE3/NR2F1 DIF protocol we observed that a large majority (&gt;99%) of normal blood and BM MNCs showed from zero up to two small NR2F1 nuclear localization signals (Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM2">

18632</a>

1864: Figure S1), and only occasionally did normal BM cells harbor up to five small signals. In contrast, in MCF7 and SKBR3 breast cancer cell line cells, and in test patient samples harboring many DTCs, a range from zero up to many, often large, irregular NR2F1 nuclear localization signals were observed, often with an appearance compatible with localization in the nucleoli (Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM2">

18652</a>

1866: Figure S1); in some DTCs cytoplasmic signals could also be observed. From our previous immunofluorescence experience in experimental models and cell lines in vivo [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Sosa MS, Parikh F, Maia AG, Estrada Y, Bosch A, Bragado P, Ekpin E, George A, Zheng Y, Lam HM, et al. NR2F1 controls tumour cell dormancy via SOX9- and RARbeta-driven quiescence programmes. Nat Commun. 2015;6:6170." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1178">

18676</a>

1868, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Fluegen G, Avivar-Valderas A, Wang Y, Padgen MR, Williams JK, Nobre AR, Calvo V, Cheung JF, Bravo-Cordero JJ, Entenberg D, et al. Phenotypic heterogeneity of disseminated tumour cells is preset by primary tumour hypoxic microenvironments. Nat Cell Biol. 2017;19(2):12032." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1182">

18698</a>

1870] we have defined NR2F1<sup>

1871high</sup>

1872 cells as cells with a strong NR2F1 signal detected in all the nuclear area (Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Fig2">

18732a</a>

1874, first row) or deposited as dotted or large irregular nucleolar-like signals (Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Fig2">

18752a</a>

1876, second row). In proliferative human and experimental tumors, the NR2F1 signal is either negative (no signal at all) or a weak speckled signal, except in certain areas that are hypoxic [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Fluegen G, Avivar-Valderas A, Wang Y, Padgen MR, Williams JK, Nobre AR, Calvo V, Cheung JF, Bravo-Cordero JJ, Entenberg D, et al. Phenotypic heterogeneity of disseminated tumour cells is preset by primary tumour hypoxic microenvironments. Nat Cell Biol. 2017;19(2):12032." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e1193">

18778</a>

1878]. Based on these data from both experimental studies and testing on MCF7 and SKBR3-spiked normal MNCs, we defined as NR2F1<sup>

1879low</sup>

1880a range of NR2F1 immunostaining from entirely negative up to five small signals as seen in normal MNCs (Additional files <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM2">

18812</a>

1882 and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM3">

18833</a>

1884: Figures S1 and S2). A NR2F1 staining &gt;5 small signals and/or large signals (1), and/or the presence of signal clusters defined DTCs as NR2F1<sup>

1885high</sup>

1886 (Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Fig2">

18872</a>

1888, Additional files <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM6">

18892</a>

1890 and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM3">

18917</a>

1892: Figures S1 and S2).</p>

1935<p>

1936In accordance with the preclinical study data presented above, we chose to classify, a priori, samples with 50% NR2F1<sup>

1937high</sup>

1938 DTCs as dormant and samples with &lt;50% NR2F1<sup>

1939high</sup>

1940 DTCs as non-dormant.</p>

1941<p>

1942One of the patients with DTC-negative status according to the original DTC analysis had one detectable DTC by the DIF analysis and was not classified according to dormant versus non-dormant status.</p>

1943<p>

1944A Ki67-expressing DTC was defined as a cell exhibiting nuclear immunostaining of Ki67.</p>

1945<h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec8">

1946Statistics</h3>

1947<p>

1948The association between DTC status/characteristics and distant disease-free interval (DFI) was analyzed. Distant DFI was defined as survival without distant breast cancer recurrence or breast cancer death, and was constructed using Kaplan-Meier curves with accompanied <i>

1949P</i>

1950 values obtained from a log-rank test. SPSS software was used for statistical analysis.</p>

1954<section data-title="Results">

1955<div class="c-article-section" id="Sec9-section">

1956<h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec9">

1957Results</h2>

1958<div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec9-content">

1959<p>

1960Bone marrow cytospins from 86 DTC-positive patients identified by the original DTC staining procedure were analyzed by DIF for cytokeratin (AE1/AE3) and NR2F1 expression as described in <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="section anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Sec2">

1961Materials and methods</a>

1962. An overview of the BM aspiration (BMA) time points for the included patients is presented in Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Fig1">

19631</a>

1964. From 24 of these patients, BM samples at 2 time points were available for DIF analysis.</p>

1965<p>

1966Cytokeratin-positive cells were classified as either NR2F1<sup>

1967high</sup>

1968 or NR2F1<sup>

1969low</sup>

1970 according to the level and pattern of expression (see <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="section anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Sec2">

1971Materials and methods</a>

1972, Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Fig2">

19732</a>

1974, and Additional files <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM2">

19752</a>

1976 and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM3">

19773</a>

1978: Figures S1 and S2).</p>

1979<p>

1980Expression of Ki67 was analyzed in parallel with the NR2F1 analyses on additional available cytospins from 15 DTC-positive patients (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Tab1">

19811</a>

1982 and Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Fig2">

19832b</a>

1984). Of the total 103 samples found to be DTC-positive (i.e., 1 detectable DTC) by the original DTC staining procedure (of 210<sup>

19856</sup>

1986 BM MNCs), 32 (31%) had cytokeratin-detectable DTCs in the DIF analysis (of 110<sup>

19876</sup>

1988 BM MNCs) (Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM4">

19894</a>

1990: Table S2), in accordance with an expected lower sensitivity of this analysis. Twenty-four samples submitted to DIF had been concluded as DTC-negative by the original DTC analysis. These included 13 samples from 11 patients with no original detectable DTCs. One of the samples had one detectable DTC by DIF, and the remaining 23 were DTC-negative (Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM4">

19914</a>

1992: Table S2). Data on the original DTC-positive patients with DIF-positive results and available clinicopathological characteristics are presented in Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Tab1">

19931</a>

1994.</p>

1995<div class="c-article-table" data-test="inline-table" data-container-section="table" id="table-1">

2013<p>

2014The DIF analysis revealed that most of the analyzed patients (24 out of 26) with CK-positive DTCs had 3 detectable cells and 16 had 10 DTCs in at least one BM sample, representing a patient group with high risk of metastasis (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Tab1">

20151</a>

2016, Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM5">

20175</a>

2018: Table S3). Indeed, 81% of the DTC-positive patients developed metastasis after the BMA (<i>

2019n</i>

2020=17) or had metastasis at time of the BM aspiration (<i>

2021n</i>

2022=4) (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Tab1">

20231</a>

2024). Half (<i>

2025n</i>

2026=13) of the patients had &gt;1% of NR2F1<sup>

2027high</sup>

2028 DTCs in at least one BM sample and 26.9% (<i>

2029n</i>

2030=7) had 50% NR2F1<sup>

2031high</sup>

2032 DTCs. The latter parameter (50% NR2F1<sup>

2033high</sup>

2034 DTCs) was chosen as the a priori cut-off for classifying the patient as having a dormant profile in accordance with previous experimental studies [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Sosa MS, Parikh F, Maia AG, Estrada Y, Bosch A, Bragado P, Ekpin E, George A, Zheng Y, Lam HM, et al. NR2F1 controls tumour cell dormancy via SOX9- and RARbeta-driven quiescence programmes. Nat Commun. 2015;6:6170." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e3639">

20356</a>

2036, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Fluegen G, Avivar-Valderas A, Wang Y, Padgen MR, Williams JK, Nobre AR, Calvo V, Cheung JF, Bravo-Cordero JJ, Entenberg D, et al. Phenotypic heterogeneity of disseminated tumour cells is preset by primary tumour hypoxic microenvironments. Nat Cell Biol. 2017;19(2):12032." href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d33543424e3643">

20378</a>

2038]. Of the samples with detectable NR2F1<sup>

2039high</sup>

2040 DTCs, the median proportion of NR2F1<sup>

2041high</sup>

2042 DTCs was 50%.</p>

2043<p>

2044To explore changes in the expression of NR2F1 over time and during treatment, DIF analysis was performed on the 24 cases classified as DTC-positive in the original DTC staining procedure and with available samples from BM aspiration at two time points (see Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM6">

20456</a>

2046: Figure S3 for the original DTC staining results). Of the cases analyzed, 16 received chemotherapy ( endocrine treatment), 5 endocrine treatment only, and 3 no systemic treatment between the BM aspirations (Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM7">

20477</a>

2048: Table S4). The number of DIF-detected CK-positive DTCs and proportion of NR2F1<sup>

2049high</sup>

2050 DTCs are presented in Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Fig3">

20513</a>

2052. The results showed different patterns of change and did not appear to be related to the type of adjuvant treatment (Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Fig3">

20533</a>

2054). Three of the six patients with 50% NR2F1<sup>

2055high</sup>

2056 DTCs at the last BM analysis did not experience relapse. In contrast, 7 of 8 patients with 1% NR2F1<sup>

2057high</sup>

2058 DTCs at the last BM analysis had systemic relapse or breast cancer death within 12months (i.e., &lt;8months) (Fig.<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Fig3">

20593b, c</a>

2060). Additional information on the original DTC status, NR2F1 expression, and Ki67 expression of these patients are presented in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#MOESM8">

20618</a>

2062 (Table S5). All patients with systemic relapse or breast cancer death within 12months had 1% NR2F1<sup>

2063high</sup>

2064 DTCs (Table<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13058-018-1049-0#Tab1">

20651</a>

2066).</p>
